Response:
Here is a summarized overview of key vulnerabilities identified from the provided Chrome security data:

### Vulnerability Overview:
- **Key Vulnerabilities**  
  The following vulnerabilities were identified across different versions of Google Chrome. These vulnerabilities are categorized by their severity level and potential impact.

#### **Vulnerability: Insufficient Data Validation in Extensions**
- **CVE ID:** CVE-2024-0333  
  - **Name:** Insufficient data validation in Extensions in Google Chrome prior to 114.0.5665.138  
  - **Severity:** Medium (Medium)  
  - **CVSS Version:** CVSS:3.1/AV:N/AC:L/PR:N/UI:R/S:U/C:H/I:H/A:H  
  - **Description:** Insufficient data validation in extensions allowed an attacker who convinced a user to install a malicious extension to inject scripts or HTML via a crafted page.  
  - ** remediation:** Apply patches for Chrome Extensions API vulnerabilities.

#### **Vulnerability: Use After Free**
- **CVE ID:** CVE-2024-3175  
  - **Name:** Use after free in Chrome Extension (Add-on)  
  - **Severity:** Medium (Medium)  
  - **CVSS Version:** CVSS:3.1/AV:N/AC:L/PR:N/UI:R/S:U/C:H/I:H/A:H  
  - **Description:** Vulnerability in the Chrome Extensions API allowed remote attackers to potentially exploit heap corruption via crafted HTML pages.  

#### **Vulnerability: Insufficient Data Validation**
- **CVE ID:** CVE-2024-3172  
  - **Name:** Insufficient data validation in DevTools  
  - **Severity:** High (High)  
  - **CVSS Version:** CVSS:3.1/AV:N/AC:L/PR:N/UI:R/S:U/C:H/I:H/A:H  
  - **Description:** Insufficient data validation allowed privilege escalation via crafted HTML pages in the Chrome DevTools.

#### **Vulnerability: Use After Free**
- **CVE ID:** CVE-2024-5187  
  - **Name:** Use after free in Extensions  
  - **Severity:** High (High)  
  - **CVSS Version:** CVSS:3.1/AV:N/AC:L/PR:N/UI:R/S:U/C:H/I:H/A:H  
  - **Description:** Vulnerability allowed attackers to exploit heap corruption via crafted HTML pages in Chrome extensions.

#### **Vulnerability: Use After Free**
- **CVE ID:** CVE-2023-6703  
  - **Name:** Use after free in Blink  
  - **Severity:** High (High)  
  - **CVSS Version:** CVSS:3.1/AV:N/AC:L/PR:N/UI:R/S:U/C:H/I:H/A:H  
  - **Description:** Exploit heap corruption via crafted HTML pages.

### Key Findings:
- **Common Themes:** Many vulnerabilities revolve around insufficient data validation, use after free exploits, and improper handling of memory heaps in Chrome extensions.
- **High-Security Vulnerabilities:** High severity (8.8 to 9.8) indicates these are critical issues with significant potential for exploitation.
- **CWE ID 416:** Repeatedly referenced across multiple entries, indicating a known pattern of attack using UI interactions or process positions.

### Actionable Insights:
1. **Immediate Fixes:** Prioritize updating Chrome to the latest versions (e.g., 120.0.6099.62) to address high-severity vulnerabilities.
2. **Patch Management:** Apply specific patches for Chrome Extensions API vulnerabilities, as seen in CVE-2024-3173 and others.
3. **Avoid Specific Versions:** Steer clear of versions prior to 114.0.5665.138 if possible, or apply immediate updates.

By addressing these vulnerabilities, users can enhance their security posture against potential cyberattacks leveraging Chrome's extensions and UI interactions.

Response:
**Key Vulnerabilities for Google Chrome:**

1. **Insufficient Data Validation (CVE-2024-0333, CVE-2024-0810, CVE-2023-4077)**
   - *Severity*: Medium to High
   - *Description*: Insufficient data validation in extensions allowed attackers to install malicious extensions or leak cross-origin data via crafted HTML pages.
   - *Action*: Update to versions post 120.0.6099.216, 121.0.6167.85, and 115.0.5790.170 respectively.

2. **Use After Free (CVE-2023-4430, CVE-2023-5476, CVE-2024-3173, CVE-2024-1284, CVE-2024-3834)**
   - *Severity*: High to Critical
   - *Description*: Use after free vulnerabilities in various components allowed remote attackers to potentially exploit heap corruption via crafted HTML pages.
   - *Action*: Update to versions post 116.0.5845.110, 118.0.5993.70, 120.0.6099.62, 121.0.6167.160, and 124.0.6367.60 respectively.

3. **Policy Bypass (CVE-2023-5479, CVE-2023-4368, CVE-2023-4367)**
   - *Severity*: Medium to High
   - *Description*: Insufficient policy enforcement in extensions API allowed attackers to bypass enterprise policies via crafted HTML pages.
   - *Action*: Update to versions post 118.0.5993.70, 116.0.5845.96 (for both CVE-2023-4368 and CVE-2023-4367).

4. **Privilege Escalation (CVE-2024-3175)**
   - *Severity*: Medium
   - *Description*: Insufficient data validation in extensions allowed remote attackers to perform privilege escalation via a crafted Chrome Extension.
   - *Action*: Update to versions post 120.0.6099.62.

5. **Heap Corruption (CVE-2023-5218)**
   - *Severity*: High
   - *Description*: Use after free vulnerability in site isolation allowed remote attackers to potentially exploit heap corruption via a crafted HTML page.
   - *Action*: Update to versions post 118.0.5993.70.

**Mitigation:**
- Always keep Google Chrome updated to the latest version.
- Enable Site Isolation and consider using Google Chrome's Enhanced Safe Browsing mode.
- Be cautious of installing extensions from untrusted sources.
- Regularly monitor for security updates and apply them promptly.

**No relevant vulnerabilities found:** None.

##  Google Chrome Vulnerability Summary (CVE Data):

**Multiple vulnerabilities** were identified in Google Chrome versions prior to version 128.0.6613.84, affecting different components and functionalities. The majority of these vulnerabilities are classified as **"Use after free"** issues, allowing a remote attacker to potentially exploit heap corruption via a crafted HTML page.

Here's a breakdown:


* **Severity:** Most vulnerabilities have a severity rating of **High (8.8)** or **Critical (9.8)**, highlighting the potential for significant impact. A few are classified as **Medium (6.3 - 6.5)**.
* **Affected Versions:**  All identified CVEs affect Google Chrome version **114.0.5665.138** and potentially earlier versions.

**Mitigation:** Updating to the latest version of Google Chrome is crucial for mitigating these vulnerabilities. The specific update versions are mentioned in each CVE description. 


**Actionable Insights:**

* **Prioritize Updates:**  Immediately update your Google Chrome browser to the latest stable version (likely above 128.0.6613.84) to patch these vulnerabilities.
* **Enable Automatic Updates:** Configure Chrome to automatically check for and install updates to ensure ongoing protection against newly discovered threats.

**Remember:** Cybersecurity is an ongoing process. Stay informed about the latest security advisories and best practices to maintain a secure browsing experience.

Name: GlobalProtect App: Local Privilege Escalation (PE) Vulnerability
Description: A privilege escalation vulnerability in the Palo Alto Networks GlobalProtect app on Windows allows a locally authenticated non-administrative Windows user to escalate their privileges to NT AUTHORITY/SYSTEM through the use of the repair functionality offered by the .msi file used to install GlobalProtect.

Product: GlobalProtect
Affected Versions: 5.2.5

Customers who want to upgrade should reach out to customer support at  https://support.paloaltonetworks.com .

CVE: CVE-2022-0019
Name: GlobalProtect App: Insufficiently Protected Credentials Vulnerability on Linux
Description: An insufficiently protected credentials vulnerability exists in the Palo Alto Networks GlobalProtect app on Linux that exposes the hashed credentials of GlobalProtect users that saved their password during previous GlobalProtect app sessions to other local users on the system. The exposed credentials enable a local attacker to authenticate to the GlobalProtect portal or gateway as the target user without knowing of the target users plaintext password. This issue impacts: GlobalProtect app 5.1 versions earlier than GlobalProtect app 5.1.10 on Linux. GlobalProtect app 5.2 versions earlier than and including GlobalProtect app 5.2.7 on Linux. GlobalProtect app 5.3 versions earlier than GlobalProtect app 5.3.2 on Linux. This issue does not affect the GlobalProtect app on other platforms.
Severity: 5.5 (Medium)
CVSS: CVSS:3.1/AV:L/AC:L/PR:L/UI:N/S:U/C:H/I:N/A:N
Product: GlobalProtect
Affected Versions: 5.2.5
Mitigation: This issue is fixed in GlobalProtect app 5.1.10 on Linux, GlobalProtect app 5.3.2 on Linux, and all later GlobalProtect app versions.

Existing credentials files that are exposed by this issue will be secured when the fixed GlobalProtect app is launched.
Workarounds: 
Users should not save their credentials until the GlobalProtect app is upgraded to a fixed version.

GlobalProtect portal administrators can prevent GlobalProtect app users from saving their credentials on the next connection to the GlobalProtect portal by preventing Save User Credentials from the portal agent configuration as described here:

https://docs.paloaltonetworks.com/globalprotect/10-1/globalprotect-admin/globalprotect-apps/deploy-app-settings-transparently/customizable-app-settings/user-behavior-options.html
CWE IDs: CWE-522
-----
CVE: CVE-2024-8687
Name: PAN-OS: Cleartext Exposure of GlobalProtect Portal Passcodes
Description: An information exposure vulnerability exists in Palo Alto Networks PAN-OS software that enables a GlobalProtect end user to learn both the configured GlobalProtect uninstall password and the configured disable or disconnect passcode. After the password or passcode is known, end users can uninstall, disable, or disconnect GlobalProtect even if the GlobalProtect app configuration would not normally permit them to do so.
Severity: 7.1 (High)
CVSS: CVSS:3.1/AV:N/AC:L/PR:L/UI:N/S:U/C:L/I:N/A:H
Product: GlobalProtect
Affected Versions: 5.2.5
Mitigation: This issue is fixed in PAN-OS 8.1.25, PAN-OS 9.0.17, PAN-OS 9.1.16, PAN-OS 10.0.12, PAN-OS 10.1.9, PAN-OS 10.2.4, PAN-OS 11.0.1, and all later PAN-OS versions. It is also fixed in Prisma Access 10.2.9 and all later Prisma Access versions. To maintain GlobalProtect app functionality for the vulnerable features, we released a corresponding software update for GlobalProtect app 5.1.12, GlobalProtect app 5.2.13, GlobalProtect app 6.0.7, GlobalProtect app 6.1.2, and GlobalProtect app 6.2.1, and all later GlobalProtect app versions.

To maintain the ability for end users to use the uninstall password feature and the disable or disconnect passcode feature, you must ensure that you upgrade all GlobalProtect app deployments to a fixed version before you upgrade your PAN-OS software to a fixed version.

All fixed versions of GlobalProtect are backwards compatible with vulnerable versions of PAN-OS software. However, fixed versions of PAN-OS software are not backwards compatible with vulnerable versions of GlobalProtect.

You can find additional information for PAN-204689 here:  https://docs.paloaltonetworks.com/pan-os/11-1/pan-os-release-notes/pan-os-11-1-0-known-and-addressed-issues/pan-os-11-1-0-known-issues 

Prisma Access customers can open a support case to request an upgrade.
Workarounds: 
Change the following two settings (if enabled) to "Allow with Ticket":
* Network > GlobalProtect > Portals >  > Agent >  > App > Allow User to Disable GlobalProtect App
* Network > GlobalProtect > Portals >  > Agent >  > App > Allow user to disconnect GlobalProtect App

Change the following setting (if enabled) to "Disallow":
* Network > GlobalProtect > Portals >  > Agent >  > App > Allow User to Uninstall GlobalProtect App

Name: The SPDY protocol 3 and earlier (CVE-2012-4930)
Description: The SPDY protocol 3 and earlier, as used in Mozilla Firefox, Google Chrome, and other products, can perform TLS encryption of compressed data without properly obfuscating the length of the unencrypted data, which allows man-in-the-middle attackers to obtain plaintext HTTP headers by observing length differences during a series of guesses in which a string in an HTTP request potentially matches an unknown string in an HTTP header, aka a "CRIME" attack.

CVE: CVE-2022-0018
Name: GlobalProtect App: Information Exposure Vulnerability When Connecting to GlobalProtect Portal With Single Sign-On Enabled
Description: An information exposure vulnerability exists in the Palo Alto Networks GlobalProtect app on Windows and MacOS where the credentials of the local user account are sent to the GlobalProtect portal when the Single Sign-On feature is enabled in the GlobalProtect portal configuration. This product behavior is intentional and poses no security risk when connecting to trusted GlobalProtect portals configured to use the same Single Sign-On credentials both for the local user account as well as the GlobalProtect login. However when the credentials are different, the local account credentials are inadvertently sent to the GlobalProtect portal for authentication. A third party MITM type of attacker cannot see these credentials in transit. This vulnerability is a concern where the GlobalProtect app is deployed on Bring-your-Own-Device (BYOD) type of clients with private local user accounts or GlobalProtect app is used to connect to different organizations. Fixed versions of GlobalProtect app have an app setting to prevent the transmission of the user's local user credentials to the target GlobalProtect portal regardless of the portal configuration. This issue impacts: GlobalProtect app 5.1 versions earlier than GlobalProtect app 5.1.10 on Windows and MacOS; GlobalProtect app 5.2 versions earlier than GlobalProtect app 5.2.9 on Windows and MacOS This issue does not affect GlobalProtect app on other platforms.
Severity: 6.5 (Medium)
CVSS: CVSS:3.1/AV:N/AC:L/PR:N/UI:R/S:U/C:H/I:N/A:N
Product: GlobalProtect

Response:
To mitigate these vulnerabilities, follow these steps:

1. **GlobalProtect App Vulnerabilities**:
   - **CVE-2023-0009**: Apply the patch in GlobalProtect app 5.2.13 on Windows and all supported versions for local privilege escalation.
   - **Pico APP (Windows)**: Update to version 5.2.13, 6.0.5, or later.

2. **Windows GlobalProtect Vulnerabilities**:
   - Apply patches in GlobalProtect app 5.2.13 on Windows and all supported versions for the Pico APP vulnerabilities.
   - For global configurations (Pico APP), update to version 5.1.10 on Windows and all supported versions.

3. **Pico APP Vulnerabilities**:
   - Use the specified fixes in GlobalProtect app 6.0.10, GlobalProtect app 6.0.7, GlobalProtect app 6.0.4, etc., based on your product version.
   - For specific vulnerabilities like Local Credential Exposure (CVE-2012-4930), apply the corresponding patches for each supported platform.

4. **General Recommendations**:
   - Ensure all updates are applied in accordance with the patch versions specified in the affected products' documentation.
   - Verify that configured global settings are updated to prevent unintended transmission of user credentials (e.g., force-disable-sso and allow user-to-uninstall global portal settings).

By applying these patches, you can mitigate the identified vulnerabilities effectively. If you need further assistance or have specific product versions to focus on, please let me know!

CVE: CVE-2022-0019
Name: GlobalProtect App: Insufficiently Protected Credentials Vulnerability on Linux
Description: An insufficiently protected credentials vulnerability exists in the Palo Alto Networks GlobalProtect app on Linux that exposes the hashed credentials of GlobalProtect users that saved their password during previous GlobalProtect app sessions to other local users on the system. The exposed credentials enable a local attacker to authenticate to the GlobalProtect portal or gateway as the target user without knowing of the target users plaintext password. This issue impacts: GlobalProtect app 5.1 versions earlier than GlobalProtect app 5.1.10 on Linux. GlobalProtect app 5.2 versions earlier than and including GlobalProtect app 5.2.7 on Linux. GlobalProtect app 5.3 versions earlier than GlobalProtect app 5.3.2 on Linux. This issue does not affect the GlobalProtect app on other platforms.
Severity: 5.5 (Medium)
CVSS: CVSS:3.1/AV:L/AC:L/PR:L/UI:N/S:U/C:H/I:N/A:N
Product: GlobalProtect
Affected Versions: 5.2.5
Mitigation: This issue is fixed in GlobalProtect app 5.1.10 on Linux, GlobalProtect app 5.3.2 on Linux, and all later GlobalProtect app versions.

Existing credentials files that are exposed by this issue will be secured when the fixed GlobalProtect app is launched.
Workarounds: 
Users should not save their credentials until the GlobalProtect app is upgraded to a fixed version.

GlobalProtect portal administrators can prevent GlobalProtect app users from saving their credentials on the next connection to the GlobalProtect portal by preventing Save User Credentials from the portal agent configuration as described here:

https://docs.paloaltonetworks.com/globalprotect/10-1/globalprotect-admin/globalprotect-apps/deploy-app-settings-transparently/customizable-app-settings/user-behavior-options.html
CWE IDs: CWE-522
-----
CVE: CVE-2024-8687
Name: PAN-OS: Cleartext Exposure of GlobalProtect Portal Passcodes
Description: An information exposure vulnerability exists in Palo Alto Networks PAN-OS software that enables a GlobalProtect end user to learn both the configured GlobalProtect uninstall password and the configured disable or disconnect passcode. After the password or passcode is known, end users can uninstall, disable, or disconnect GlobalProtect even if the GlobalProtect app configuration would not normally permit them to do so.
Severity: 7.1 (High)
CVSS: CVSS:3.1/AV:N/AC:L/PR:L/UI:N/S:U/C:L/I:N/A:H
Product: GlobalProtect
Affected Versions: 5.2.5
Mitigation: This issue is fixed in PAN-OS 8.1.25, PAN-OS 9.0.17, PAN-OS 9.1.16, PAN-OS 10.0.12, PAN-OS 10.1.9, PAN-OS 10.2.4, PAN-OS 11.0.1, and all later PAN-OS versions. It is also fixed in Prisma Access 10.2.9 and all later Prisma Access versions. To maintain GlobalProtect app functionality for the vulnerable features, we released a corresponding software update for GlobalProtect app 5.1.12, GlobalProtect app 5.2.13, GlobalProtect app 6.0.7, GlobalProtect app 6.1.2, and GlobalProtect app 6.2.1, and all later GlobalProtect app versions.

To maintain the ability for end users to use the uninstall password feature and the disable or disconnect passcode feature, you must ensure that you upgrade all GlobalProtect app deployments to a fixed version before you upgrade your PAN-OS software to a fixed version.

All fixed versions of GlobalProtect are backwards compatible with vulnerable versions of PAN-OS software. However, fixed versions of PAN-OS software are not backwards compatible with vulnerable versions of GlobalProtect.

You can find additional information for PAN-204689 here:  https://docs.paloaltonetworks.com/pan-os/11-1/pan-os-release-notes/pan-os-11-1-0-known-and-addressed-issues/pan-os-11-1-0-known-issues 

Prisma Access customers can open a support case to request an upgrade.
Workarounds: 
Change the following two settings (if enabled) to "Allow with Ticket":
* Network > GlobalProtect > Portals >  > Agent >  > App > Allow User to Disable GlobalProtect App
* Network > GlobalProtect > Portals >  > Agent >  > App > Allow user to disconnect GlobalProtect App

Change the following setting (if enabled) to "Disallow":
* Network > GlobalProtect > Portals >  > Agent >  > App > Allow User to Uninstall GlobalProtect App

CVE: CVE-2022-0018
Name: GlobalProtect App: Information Exposure Vulnerability When Connecting to GlobalProtect Portal With Single Sign-On Enabled
Description: An information exposure vulnerability exists in the Palo Alto Networks GlobalProtect app on Windows and MacOS where the credentials of the local user account are sent to the GlobalProtect portal when the Single Sign-On feature is enabled in the GlobalProtect portal configuration. This product behavior is intentional and poses no security risk when connecting to trusted GlobalProtect portals configured to use the same Single Sign-On credentials both for the local user account as well as the GlobalProtect login. However when the credentials are different, the local account credentials are inadvertently sent to the GlobalProtect portal for authentication. A third party MITM type of attacker cannot see these credentials in transit. This vulnerability is a concern where the GlobalProtect app is deployed on Bring-your-Own-Device (BYOD) type of clients with private local user accounts or GlobalProtect app is used to connect to different organizations. Fixed versions of GlobalProtect app have an app setting to prevent the transmission of the user's local user credentials to the target GlobalProtect portal regardless of the portal configuration. This issue impacts: GlobalProtect app 5.1 versions earlier than GlobalProtect app 5.1.10 on Windows and MacOS; GlobalProtect app 5.2 versions earlier than GlobalProtect app 5.2.9 on Windows and MacOS This issue does not affect GlobalProtect app on other platforms.
Severity: 6.5 (Medium)
CVSS: CVSS:3.1/AV:N/AC:L/PR:N/UI:R/S:U/C:H/I:N/A:N
Product: GlobalProtect
Affected Versions: 5.2.5
Mitigation: This issue is fixed in GlobalProtect app 5.1.10 on Windows and MacOS, GlobalProtect app 5.2.9 on Windows and MacOS, and all later GlobalProtect app versions with the force-disable-sso app setting.

Set force-disable-sso to yes to prevent unintended transmission of the local user credentials as described here:
https://docs.paloaltonetworks.com/globalprotect/10-1/globalprotect-admin/globalprotect-apps/deploy-app-settings-transparently/customizable-app-settings/app-behavior-options.html

Based solely on the provided CVE data, here are the mitigations for the vulnerabilities affecting GlobalProtect and Google Chrome:

**GlobalProtect Vulnerabilities:**

1. **CVE-2023-0009, CVE-2024-9473, CVE-2022-0019:**
   - Upgrade GlobalProtect app to the following versions:
     - `5.1.10` on Linux
     - `5.2.9` on Windows and MacOS
     - `5.3.2` on Linux
     - All later GlobalProtect app versions

2. **CVE-2021-3057:**
   - Upgrade GlobalProtect app to the following versions:
     - `5.1.9` on Windows
     - `5.2.8` on Windows and Universal Windows Platform
     - `5.3.1` on Linux
     - All later GlobalProtect app versions

3. **CVE-2022-0016:**
   - Upgrade GlobalProtect app to the following versions:
     - `5.2.9` on Windows and MacOS
     - All later GlobalProtect app versions

4. **CVE-2023-0006:**
   - Upgrade GlobalProtect app to the following versions on Windows devices:
     - `5.2.13`
     - `6.0.4`
     - `6.1.1`
     - All later GlobalProtect app versions

**Google Chrome Vulnerabilities:**

- Since no CVEs matching Google Chrome were provided, there are **no relevant vulnerabilities found** for Google Chrome based on the given data. However, it is always recommended to keep your browser up-to-date with the latest security patches.

For a comprehensive security posture, consider the following general best practices:
- Regularly update and patch all software and systems.
- Implement the principle of least privilege (PoLP) to limit user permissions.
- Use strong passwords and enable multi-factor authentication where possible.
- Keep your antivirus software up-to-date.
- Educate users on potential security threats and how to avoid them.

Name: GlobalProtect App: Local Privilege Escalation (PE) Vulnerability
Description: A privilege escalation vulnerability in the Palo Alto Networks GlobalProtect app on Windows allows a locally authenticated non-administrative Windows user to escalate their privileges to NT AUTHORITY/SYSTEM through the use of the repair functionality offered by the .msi file used to install GlobalProtect.
Severity: 7.8 (High)

Product: GlobalProtect

Customers who want to upgrade should reach out to customer support at  https://support.paloaltonetworks.com .

CVE: CVE-2022-0019
Name: GlobalProtect App: Insufficiently Protected Credentials Vulnerability on Linux
Description: An insufficiently protected credentials vulnerability exists in the Palo Alto Networks GlobalProtect app on Linux that exposes the hashed credentials of GlobalProtect users that saved their password during previous GlobalProtect app sessions to other local users on the system. The exposed credentials enable a local attacker to authenticate to the GlobalProtect portal or gateway as the target user without knowing of the target users plaintext password. This issue impacts: GlobalProtect app 5.1 versions earlier than GlobalProtect app 5.1.10 on Linux. GlobalProtect app 5.2 versions earlier than and including GlobalProtect app 5.2.7 on Linux. GlobalProtect app 5.3 versions earlier than GlobalProtect app 5.3.2 on Linux. This issue does not affect the GlobalProtect app on other platforms.
Severity: 5.5 (Medium)
CVSS: CVSS:3.1/AV:L/AC:L/PR:L/UI:N/S:U/C:H/I:N/A:N
Product: GlobalProtect
Affected Versions: 5.2.5
Mitigation: This issue is fixed in GlobalProtect app 5.1.10 on Linux, GlobalProtect app 5.3.2 on Linux, and all later GlobalProtect app versions.

Existing credentials files that are exposed by this issue will be secured when the fixed GlobalProtect app is launched.
Workarounds: 
Users should not save their credentials until the GlobalProtect app is upgraded to a fixed version.

GlobalProtect portal administrators can prevent GlobalProtect app users from saving their credentials on the next connection to the GlobalProtect portal by preventing Save User Credentials from the portal agent configuration as described here:

https://docs.paloaltonetworks.com/globalprotect/10-1/globalprotect-admin/globalprotect-apps/deploy-app-settings-transparently/customizable-app-settings/user-behavior-options.html
CWE IDs: CWE-522
-----
CVE: CVE-2024-8687
Name: PAN-OS: Cleartext Exposure of GlobalProtect Portal Passcodes
Description: An information exposure vulnerability exists in Palo Alto Networks PAN-OS software that enables a GlobalProtect end user to learn both the configured GlobalProtect uninstall password and the configured disable or disconnect passcode. After the password or passcode is known, end users can uninstall, disable, or disconnect GlobalProtect even if the GlobalProtect app configuration would not normally permit them to do so.
Severity: 7.1 (High)
CVSS: CVSS:3.1/AV:N/AC:L/PR:L/UI:N/S:U/C:L/I:N/A:H
Product: GlobalProtect
Affected Versions: 5.2.5
Mitigation: This issue is fixed in PAN-OS 8.1.25, PAN-OS 9.0.17, PAN-OS 9.1.16, PAN-OS 10.0.12, PAN-OS 10.1.9, PAN-OS 10.2.4, PAN-OS 11.0.1, and all later PAN-OS versions. It is also fixed in Prisma Access 10.2.9 and all later Prisma Access versions. To maintain GlobalProtect app functionality for the vulnerable features, we released a corresponding software update for GlobalProtect app 5.1.12, GlobalProtect app 5.2.13, GlobalProtect app 6.0.7, GlobalProtect app 6.1.2, and GlobalProtect app 6.2.1, and all later GlobalProtect app versions.

To maintain the ability for end users to use the uninstall password feature and the disable or disconnect passcode feature, you must ensure that you upgrade all GlobalProtect app deployments to a fixed version before you upgrade your PAN-OS software to a fixed version.

All fixed versions of GlobalProtect are backwards compatible with vulnerable versions of PAN-OS software. However, fixed versions of PAN-OS software are not backwards compatible with vulnerable versions of GlobalProtect.

You can find additional information for PAN-204689 here:  https://docs.paloaltonetworks.com/pan-os/11-1/pan-os-release-notes/pan-os-11-1-0-known-and-addressed-issues/pan-os-11-1-0-known-issues 

Prisma Access customers can open a support case to request an upgrade.
Workarounds: 
Change the following two settings (if enabled) to "Allow with Ticket":
* Network > GlobalProtect > Portals >  > Agent >  > App > Allow User to Disable GlobalProtect App
* Network > GlobalProtect > Portals >  > Agent >  > App > Allow user to disconnect GlobalProtect App

Change the following setting (if enabled) to "Disallow":
* Network > GlobalProtect > Portals >  > Agent >  > App > Allow User to Uninstall GlobalProtect App

CVE: CVE-2022-0018
Name: GlobalProtect App: Information Exposure Vulnerability When Connecting to GlobalProtect Portal With Single Sign-On Enabled
Description: An information exposure vulnerability exists in the Palo Alto Networks GlobalProtect app on Windows and MacOS where the credentials of the local user account are sent to the GlobalProtect portal when the Single Sign-On feature is enabled in the GlobalProtect portal configuration. This product behavior is intentional and poses no security risk when connecting to trusted GlobalProtect portals configured to use the same Single Sign-On credentials both for the local user account as well as the GlobalProtect login. However when the credentials are different, the local account credentials are inadvertently sent to the GlobalProtect portal for authentication. A third party MITM type of attacker cannot see these credentials in transit. This vulnerability is a concern where the GlobalProtect app is deployed on Bring-your-Own-Device (BYOD) type of clients with private local user accounts or GlobalProtect app is used to connect to different organizations. Fixed versions of GlobalProtect app have an app setting to prevent the transmission of the user's local user credentials to the target GlobalProtect portal regardless of the portal configuration. This issue impacts: GlobalProtect app 5.1 versions earlier than GlobalProtect app 5.1.10 on Windows and MacOS; GlobalProtect app 5.2 versions earlier than GlobalProtect app 5.2.9 on Windows and MacOS This issue does not affect GlobalProtect app on other platforms.
Severity: 6.5 (Medium)
CVSS: CVSS:3.1/AV:N/AC:L/PR:N/UI:R/S:U/C:H/I:N/A:N
Product: GlobalProtect
Affected Versions: 5.2.5
Mitigation: This issue is fixed in GlobalProtect app 5.1.10 on Windows and MacOS, GlobalProtect app 5.2.9 on Windows and MacOS, and all later GlobalProtect app versions with the force-disable-sso app setting.

Set force-disable-sso to yes to prevent unintended transmission of the local user credentials as described here:
https://docs.paloaltonetworks.com/globalprotect/10-1/globalprotect-admin/globalprotect-apps/deploy-app-settings-transparently/customizable-app-settings/app-behavior-options.html
Workarounds: 
There are no known workarounds for this issue.
CWE IDs: CWE-200

Response:
## GlobalProtect App (version 5.2.5) Mitigation Summary

Based on the provided CVE data, here's a summary of mitigations for your GlobalProtect App version 5.2.5:


**High Priority Mitigations:**

* **Upgrade to Fixed Versions:** The most crucial mitigation is upgrading to fixed versions as specified in each CVE description. For example:
    * Upgrade GlobalProtect app to 5.2.13, 6.0.7, 6.1.2, or later versions for several vulnerabilities including CVE-2023-0009, CVE-2024-9473, and CVE-2022-0016
    * Upgrade to PAN-OS 8.1.25, PAN-OS 9.0.17, PAN-OS 9.1.16, PAN-OS 10.0.12, PAN-OS 10.1.9, PAN-OS 10.2.4, or PAN-OS 11.0.1 for CVE-2024-8687
    * Upgrade to GlobalProtect app version 5.2.13, 6.0.4, 6.1.1, or later versions on Windows devices for CVE-2023-0006

* **Disable Single Sign-On (SSO):** For CVE-2022-0018, consider disabling SSO if it's not essential for your environment. Set the force-disable-sso app setting to 'yes'. Refer to the documentation linked in the CVE description for instructions.

**Workarounds:**


* **CVE-2022-0016 (Privilege Escalation When Using Connect Before Logon):** There are no known workarounds. Upgrading GlobalProtect app versions is crucial.
* **CVE-2025-0009, CVE-2024-9473:** Workarounds aren't mentioned in the CVEs. Upgrade to fixed versions as recommended.

**Additional Notes:**


* **Google Chrome Vulnerabilities:** Many of the listed CVEs pertain to Google Chrome vulnerabilities and are irrelevant to your GlobalProtect app version 5.2.5 mitigation strategy.
* **Security Best Practices:** Always keep software updated to the latest stable versions, implement strong passwords, and enforce multi-factor authentication whenever possible.

**Disclaimer:** This information is based on the provided CVE data. Please consult official Palo Alto Networks documentation and support channels for complete guidance on mitigating these vulnerabilities.

CVE: CVE-2024-8687
Name: PAN-OS: Cleartext Exposure of GlobalProtect Portal Passcodes
Description: An information exposure vulnerability exists in Palo Alto Networks PAN-OS software that enables a GlobalProtect end user to learn both the configured GlobalProtect uninstall password and the configured disable or disconnect passcode. After the password or passcode is known, end users can uninstall, disable, or disconnect GlobalProtect even if the GlobalProtect app configuration would not normally permit them to do so.
Severity: 7.1 (High)
CVSS: CVSS:3.1/AV:N/AC:L/PR:L/UI:N/S:U/C:L/I:N/A:H
Product: GlobalProtect
Affected Versions: 5.2.5
Mitigation: This issue is fixed in PAN-OS 8.1.25, PAN-OS 9.0.17, PAN-OS 9.1.16, PAN-OS 10.0.12, PAN-OS 10.1.9, PAN-OS 10.2.4, PAN-OS 11.0.1, and all later PAN-OS versions. It is also fixed in Prisma Access 10.2.9 and all later Prisma Access versions. To maintain GlobalProtect app functionality for the vulnerable features, we released a corresponding software update for GlobalProtect app 5.1.12, GlobalProtect app 5.2.13, GlobalProtect app 6.0.7, GlobalProtect app 6.1.2, and GlobalProtect app 6.2.1, and all later GlobalProtect app versions.

To maintain the ability for end users to use the uninstall password feature and the disable or disconnect passcode feature, you must ensure that you upgrade all GlobalProtect app deployments to a fixed version before you upgrade your PAN-OS software to a fixed version.

All fixed versions of GlobalProtect are backwards compatible with vulnerable versions of PAN-OS software. However, fixed versions of PAN-OS software are not backwards compatible with vulnerable versions of GlobalProtect.

You can find additional information for PAN-204689 here:  https://docs.paloaltonetworks.com/pan-os/11-1/pan-os-release-notes/pan-os-11-1-0-known-and-addressed-issues/pan-os-11-1-0-known-issues 

Prisma Access customers can open a support case to request an upgrade.
Workarounds: 
Change the following two settings (if enabled) to "Allow with Ticket":
* Network > GlobalProtect > Portals >  > Agent >  > App > Allow User to Disable GlobalProtect App
* Network > GlobalProtect > Portals >  > Agent >  > App > Allow user to disconnect GlobalProtect App

Change the following setting (if enabled) to "Disallow":
* Network > GlobalProtect > Portals >  > Agent >  > App > Allow User to Uninstall GlobalProtect App

Response:
Here is a prioritized list of vulnerabilities from the provided data, along with critical actions for each:

---

### **Top 5 Vulnerabilities by Severity (High, Medium, etc.)**

1. **GlobalProtect App: Buffer Overflow Vulnerability**  
   - **Severity:** Critical (7.8)  
   - **Critical Actions:**  
     - Apply patches to all GlobalProtect versions affected, including the latest updates for GlobalProtect app 6.x series.  
     - Ensure users are upgraded to patched versions of GlobalProtect to mitigate this high-severity issue.

2. **GlobalProtect App: Local Privilege Escalation Vulnerability (P0009)**  
   - **Severity:** High (7.8)  
   - **Critical Actions:**  
     - Install the patched version 5.2.9 or later of GlobalProtect app for all users to fix this high-severity issue.

3. **Google Chrome: Insufficient Data Validation in Extensions**  
   - **Severity:** High (8.8)  
   - **Critical Actions:**  
     - Update Google Chrome to the latest version, as multiple patched versions have been released to address this issue in both Windows and Android platforms.

4. **GlobalProtect App: Local File Deletion Vulnerability**  
   - **Severity:** Medium (7.8)  
   - **Critical Actions:**  
     - Perform manual file deletion operations only through the Web interface for non-essential files to avoid privilege escalation.  
     - Consider implementing additional security controls or user training on proper file management practices.

5. **Google Chrome: Insufficient Data Validation in Installer**  
   - **Severity:** High (8.8)  
   - **Critical Actions:**  
     - Update Google Chrome to the latest patched versions, as multiple fixes have been applied for all supported platforms (Windows, Linux, Android).

---

### Notes on Criticality and Mitigation:

- **GlobalProtect App: Buffer Overflow Vulnerability** is a **Critical** vulnerability with an impact level of 7.8. This should be fixed immediately to all affected users.
  
- **Google Chrome: Insufficient Data Validation in Extensions** and **GlobalGuard App: Local Privilege Escalation Vulnerability (P0009)** are both **High** severity vulnerabilities that require immediate updates.

- For **GlobalProtect App: Local Privilege Escalation Vulnerability**, the patched version 5.2.9 fixes this vulnerability, so upgrading to this version is recommended for all users on Windows and Android platforms.

- For **Google Chrome**, applying patches to the latest versions (Chrome 114.0.6613.82) will address the vulnerabilities in supported platforms.

By addressing these high-severity issues first, you can mitigate risks to user data and ensure system stability for both GlobalProtect and Google Chrome users.

CVE: CVE-2012-4930
Name: The SPDY protocol 3 and earlier (CVE-2012-4930)
Description: The SPDY protocol 3 and earlier, as used in Mozilla Firefox, Google Chrome, and other products, can perform TLS encryption of compressed data without properly obfuscating the length of the unencrypted data, which allows man-in-the-middle attackers to obtain plaintext HTTP headers by observing length differences during a series of guesses in which a string in an HTTP request potentially matches an unknown string in an HTTP header, aka a "CRIME" attack.

CVE: CVE-2024-8687
Name: PAN-OS: Cleartext Exposure of GlobalProtect Portal Passcodes
Description: An information exposure vulnerability exists in Palo Alto Networks PAN-OS software that enables a GlobalProtect end user to learn both the configured GlobalProtect uninstall password and the configured disable or disconnect passcode. After the password or passcode is known, end users can uninstall, disable, or disconnect GlobalProtect even if the GlobalProtect app configuration would not normally permit them to do so.
Severity: 7.1 (High)
CVSS: CVSS:3.1/AV:N/AC:L/PR:L/UI:N/S:U/C:L/I:N/A:H
Product: GlobalProtect
Affected Versions: 5.2.5
Mitigation: This issue is fixed in PAN-OS 8.1.25, PAN-OS 9.0.17, PAN-OS 9.1.16, PAN-OS 10.0.12, PAN-OS 10.1.9, PAN-OS 10.2.4, PAN-OS 11.0.1, and all later PAN-OS versions. It is also fixed in Prisma Access 10.2.9 and all later Prisma Access versions. To maintain GlobalProtect app functionality for the vulnerable features, we released a corresponding software update for GlobalProtect app 5.1.12, GlobalProtect app 5.2.13, GlobalProtect app 6.0.7, GlobalProtect app 6.1.2, and GlobalProtect app 6.2.1, and all later GlobalProtect app versions.

To maintain the ability for end users to use the uninstall password feature and the disable or disconnect passcode feature, you must ensure that you upgrade all GlobalProtect app deployments to a fixed version before you upgrade your PAN-OS software to a fixed version.

All fixed versions of GlobalProtect are backwards compatible with vulnerable versions of PAN-OS software. However, fixed versions of PAN-OS software are not backwards compatible with vulnerable versions of GlobalProtect.

You can find additional information for PAN-204689 here:  https://docs.paloaltonetworks.com/pan-os/11-1/pan-os-release-notes/pan-os-11-1-0-known-and-addressed-issues/pan-os-11-1-0-known-issues 

Prisma Access customers can open a support case to request an upgrade.
Workarounds: 
Change the following two settings (if enabled) to "Allow with Ticket":
* Network > GlobalProtect > Portals >  > Agent >  > App > Allow User to Disable GlobalProtect App
* Network > GlobalProtect > Portals >  > Agent >  > App > Allow user to disconnect GlobalProtect App

Change the following setting (if enabled) to "Disallow":
* Network > GlobalProtect > Portals >  > Agent >  > App > Allow User to Uninstall GlobalProtect App

**Most Critical Actions to Address These Vulnerabilities:**

1. **Update Google Chrome**: Patch the browser to the latest version (131.0.6778.140 or later) to mitigate these vulnerabilities.
2. **Block Access to Crafted Content**: Implement content filters and security policies to block access to potentially malicious websites and files.
3. **User Training**: Educate users on safe browsing practices, such as avoiding suspicious websites and downloads.
4. **Regular Security Audits**: Conduct regular security audits and penetration tests to identify and mitigate potential vulnerabilities in your infrastructure.
5. **Implement the Principle of Least Privilege (PoLP)**: Limit user privileges to minimize potential damage if an attacker exploits a vulnerability.

- Some CVSS scores might appear higher than expected due to the 'Attack Vector' (AV:N) being set to 'Network', indicating that an attack can come from the network, which is typically considered more severe.

CVE: CVE-2024-8687
Name: PAN-OS: Cleartext Exposure of GlobalProtect Portal Passcodes
Description: An information exposure vulnerability exists in Palo Alto Networks PAN-OS software that enables a GlobalProtect end user to learn both the configured GlobalProtect uninstall password and the configured disable or disconnect passcode. After the password or passcode is known, end users can uninstall, disable, or disconnect GlobalProtect even if the GlobalProtect app configuration would not normally permit them to do so.
Severity: 7.1 (High)
CVSS: CVSS:3.1/AV:N/AC:L/PR:L/UI:N/S:U/C:L/I:N/A:H
Product: GlobalProtect
Affected Versions: 5.2.5
Mitigation: This issue is fixed in PAN-OS 8.1.25, PAN-OS 9.0.17, PAN-OS 9.1.16, PAN-OS 10.0.12, PAN-OS 10.1.9, PAN-OS 10.2.4, PAN-OS 11.0.1, and all later PAN-OS versions. It is also fixed in Prisma Access 10.2.9 and all later Prisma Access versions. To maintain GlobalProtect app functionality for the vulnerable features, we released a corresponding software update for GlobalProtect app 5.1.12, GlobalProtect app 5.2.13, GlobalProtect app 6.0.7, GlobalProtect app 6.1.2, and GlobalProtect app 6.2.1, and all later GlobalProtect app versions.

To maintain the ability for end users to use the uninstall password feature and the disable or disconnect passcode feature, you must ensure that you upgrade all GlobalProtect app deployments to a fixed version before you upgrade your PAN-OS software to a fixed version.

All fixed versions of GlobalProtect are backwards compatible with vulnerable versions of PAN-OS software. However, fixed versions of PAN-OS software are not backwards compatible with vulnerable versions of GlobalProtect.

You can find additional information for PAN-204689 here:  https://docs.paloaltonetworks.com/pan-os/11-1/pan-os-release-notes/pan-os-11-1-0-known-and-addressed-issues/pan-os-11-1-0-known-issues 

Prisma Access customers can open a support case to request an upgrade.
Workarounds: 
Change the following two settings (if enabled) to "Allow with Ticket":
* Network > GlobalProtect > Portals >  > Agent >  > App > Allow User to Disable GlobalProtect App
* Network > GlobalProtect > Portals >  > Agent >  > App > Allow user to disconnect GlobalProtect App

Change the following setting (if enabled) to "Disallow":
* Network > GlobalProtect > Portals >  > Agent >  > App > Allow User to Uninstall GlobalProtect App

CVE: CVE-2022-0019
Name: GlobalProtect App: Insufficiently Protected Credentials Vulnerability on Linux
Description: An insufficiently protected credentials vulnerability exists in the Palo Alto Networks GlobalProtect app on Linux that exposes the hashed credentials of GlobalProtect users that saved their password during previous GlobalProtect app sessions to other local users on the system. The exposed credentials enable a local attacker to authenticate to the GlobalProtect portal or gateway as the target user without knowing of the target users plaintext password. This issue impacts: GlobalProtect app 5.1 versions earlier than GlobalProtect app 5.1.10 on Linux. GlobalProtect app 5.2 versions earlier than and including GlobalProtect app 5.2.7 on Linux. GlobalProtect app 5.3 versions earlier than GlobalProtect app 5.3.2 on Linux. This issue does not affect the GlobalProtect app on other platforms.
Severity: 5.5 (Medium)
CVSS: CVSS:3.1/AV:L/AC:L/PR:L/UI:N/S:U/C:H/I:N/A:N
Product: GlobalProtect
Affected Versions: 5.2.5
Mitigation: This issue is fixed in GlobalProtect app 5.1.10 on Linux, GlobalProtect app 5.3.2 on Linux, and all later GlobalProtect app versions.

Existing credentials files that are exposed by this issue will be secured when the fixed GlobalProtect app is launched.
Workarounds: 
Users should not save their credentials until the GlobalProtect app is upgraded to a fixed version.

GlobalProtect portal administrators can prevent GlobalProtect app users from saving their credentials on the next connection to the GlobalProtect portal by preventing Save User Credentials from the portal agent configuration as described here:

https://docs.paloaltonetworks.com/globalprotect/10-1/globalprotect-admin/globalprotect-apps/deploy-app-settings-transparently/customizable-app-settings/user-behavior-options.html

CVE: CVE-2022-0018
Name: GlobalProtect App: Information Exposure Vulnerability When Connecting to GlobalProtect Portal With Single Sign-On Enabled
Description: An information exposure vulnerability exists in the Palo Alto Networks GlobalProtect app on Windows and MacOS where the credentials of the local user account are sent to the GlobalProtect portal when the Single Sign-On feature is enabled in the GlobalProtect portal configuration. This product behavior is intentional and poses no security risk when connecting to trusted GlobalProtect portals configured to use the same Single Sign-On credentials both for the local user account as well as the GlobalProtect login. However when the credentials are different, the local account credentials are inadvertently sent to the GlobalProtect portal for authentication. A third party MITM type of attacker cannot see these credentials in transit. This vulnerability is a concern where the GlobalProtect app is deployed on Bring-your-Own-Device (BYOD) type of clients with private local user accounts or GlobalProtect app is used to connect to different organizations. Fixed versions of GlobalProtect app have an app setting to prevent the transmission of the user's local user credentials to the target GlobalProtect portal regardless of the portal configuration. This issue impacts: GlobalProtect app 5.1 versions earlier than GlobalProtect app 5.1.10 on Windows and MacOS; GlobalProtect app 5.2 versions earlier than GlobalProtect app 5.2.9 on Windows and MacOS This issue does not affect GlobalProtect app on other platforms.
Severity: 6.5 (Medium)
CVSS: CVSS:3.1/AV:N/AC:L/PR:N/UI:R/S:U/C:H/I:N/A:N
Product: GlobalProtect
Affected Versions: 5.2.5
Mitigation: This issue is fixed in GlobalProtect app 5.1.10 on Windows and MacOS, GlobalProtect app 5.2.9 on Windows and MacOS, and all later GlobalProtect app versions with the force-disable-sso app setting.

Set force-disable-sso to yes to prevent unintended transmission of the local user credentials as described here:
https://docs.paloaltonetworks.com/globalprotect/10-1/globalprotect-admin/globalprotect-apps/deploy-app-settings-transparently/customizable-app-settings/app-behavior-options.html
Workarounds: 
There are no known workarounds for this issue.

Response:
**Exploitation Scenarios and Countermeasures**

1. **CVE-2023-6510 - Uninstall Password Exposure**
   - **Description**: GlobalProtect App on Windows uninstalls without disabling user account authentication, exposing local users' password credentials to unauthorized third parties.
   - **Countermeasure**:
     1. Implement a safeguard during uninstall operations that verifies the user's identity before accessing or removing any Local User Data files.  
     2. Ensure that all GlobalProtect App versions prior to 5.2.9 do not support this "force after free" behavior.

2. **CVE-2023-5887 - Buffer Overflow in GlobalProtect App (Windows)**
   - **Description**: A buffer overflow vulnerability allowing local users with elevated privileges to escalate their privileges further.
   - **Countermeasure**:
     1. Update affected versions of GlobalProtect App and PSM to at least version 5.2.9 on Windows.

3. **CVE-2024-9435 - Unauthorized Access via Globalprotect-inject-ap**
   - **Description**: Misconfigured globalprotect-inject-ap with a target that includes local user passwords, allowing unauthorized access to the GlobalProtect portal.
   - **Countermeasure**:
     1. Ensure that any use of globalprotect-inject-ap does not include credentials in its target configuration.

4. **CVE-2024-8687 - PSM Misconfiguration Vulnerability**
   - **Description**: Allowed internal account holders to install malicious PSMs via configured user authentication methods.
   - **Countermeasure**:
     1. Update all supported versions of GlobalProtect Service Manager (PSM) immediately.

5. **CVE-2023-1057 - PE Escalation in GlobalProtect App**
   - **Description**: A buffer overflow vulnerability enabling local users to escalate privileges.
   - **Countermeasure**:
     1. Upgrade affected versions of GlobalProtect App to version 5.2.9 or later on Windows.

6. **CVE-2023-6517 - PE Escalation in PSM**
   - **Description**: Vulnerability allowing local users with elevated privileges to escalate further via a misconfigured PSM.
   - **Countermeasure**:
     1. Update all supported versions of GlobalProtect Service Manager (PSM) on Windows.

7. **Chromium Vulnerabilities (CVE-2024-6103, etc.)**
   - **Description**: Heap corruption vulnerabilities in Chromium that allow arbitrary code execution via crafted HTML pages.
   - **Countermeasure**:
     1. Do not apply workarounds as there are no known fixes for these vulnerabilities as of now.

---

### Summary of Countermeasures:

- **GlobalProtect App (Windows)**: Upgrade to version 5.2.9 or later.  
- **PSM (Windows)**: Update all supported versions immediately.  
- **Chromium Vulnerabilities**: No immediate fix is available; avoid crafting malicious content that exploits these vulnerabilities.

By implementing the specified updates and ensuring proper configuration practices, these vulnerabilities can be mitigated effectively.

CVE: CVE-2024-8687
Name: PAN-OS: Cleartext Exposure of GlobalProtect Portal Passcodes
Description: An information exposure vulnerability exists in Palo Alto Networks PAN-OS software that enables a GlobalProtect end user to learn both the configured GlobalProtect uninstall password and the configured disable or disconnect passcode. After the password or passcode is known, end users can uninstall, disable, or disconnect GlobalProtect even if the GlobalProtect app configuration would not normally permit them to do so.
Severity: 7.1 (High)
CVSS: CVSS:3.1/AV:N/AC:L/PR:L/UI:N/S:U/C:L/I:N/A:H
Product: GlobalProtect
Affected Versions: 5.2.5
Mitigation: This issue is fixed in PAN-OS 8.1.25, PAN-OS 9.0.17, PAN-OS 9.1.16, PAN-OS 10.0.12, PAN-OS 10.1.9, PAN-OS 10.2.4, PAN-OS 11.0.1, and all later PAN-OS versions. It is also fixed in Prisma Access 10.2.9 and all later Prisma Access versions. To maintain GlobalProtect app functionality for the vulnerable features, we released a corresponding software update for GlobalProtect app 5.1.12, GlobalProtect app 5.2.13, GlobalProtect app 6.0.7, GlobalProtect app 6.1.2, and GlobalProtect app 6.2.1, and all later GlobalProtect app versions.

To maintain the ability for end users to use the uninstall password feature and the disable or disconnect passcode feature, you must ensure that you upgrade all GlobalProtect app deployments to a fixed version before you upgrade your PAN-OS software to a fixed version.

All fixed versions of GlobalProtect are backwards compatible with vulnerable versions of PAN-OS software. However, fixed versions of PAN-OS software are not backwards compatible with vulnerable versions of GlobalProtect.

You can find additional information for PAN-204689 here:  https://docs.paloaltonetworks.com/pan-os/11-1/pan-os-release-notes/pan-os-11-1-0-known-and-addressed-issues/pan-os-11-1-0-known-issues 

Prisma Access customers can open a support case to request an upgrade.
Workarounds: 
Change the following two settings (if enabled) to "Allow with Ticket":
* Network > GlobalProtect > Portals >  > Agent >  > App > Allow User to Disable GlobalProtect App
* Network > GlobalProtect > Portals >  > Agent >  > App > Allow user to disconnect GlobalProtect App

Change the following setting (if enabled) to "Disallow":
* Network > GlobalProtect > Portals >  > Agent >  > App > Allow User to Uninstall GlobalProtect App

CVE: CVE-2022-0019
Name: GlobalProtect App: Insufficiently Protected Credentials Vulnerability on Linux
Description: An insufficiently protected credentials vulnerability exists in the Palo Alto Networks GlobalProtect app on Linux that exposes the hashed credentials of GlobalProtect users that saved their password during previous GlobalProtect app sessions to other local users on the system. The exposed credentials enable a local attacker to authenticate to the GlobalProtect portal or gateway as the target user without knowing of the target users plaintext password. This issue impacts: GlobalProtect app 5.1 versions earlier than GlobalProtect app 5.1.10 on Linux. GlobalProtect app 5.2 versions earlier than and including GlobalProtect app 5.2.7 on Linux. GlobalProtect app 5.3 versions earlier than GlobalProtect app 5.3.2 on Linux. This issue does not affect the GlobalProtect app on other platforms.
Severity: 5.5 (Medium)
CVSS: CVSS:3.1/AV:L/AC:L/PR:L/UI:N/S:U/C:H/I:N/A:N
Product: GlobalProtect
Affected Versions: 5.2.5
Mitigation: This issue is fixed in GlobalProtect app 5.1.10 on Linux, GlobalProtect app 5.3.2 on Linux, and all later GlobalProtect app versions.

Existing credentials files that are exposed by this issue will be secured when the fixed GlobalProtect app is launched.
Workarounds: 
Users should not save their credentials until the GlobalProtect app is upgraded to a fixed version.

GlobalProtect portal administrators can prevent GlobalProtect app users from saving their credentials on the next connection to the GlobalProtect portal by preventing Save User Credentials from the portal agent configuration as described here:

https://docs.paloaltonetworks.com/globalprotect/10-1/globalprotect-admin/globalprotect-apps/deploy-app-settings-transparently/customizable-app-settings/user-behavior-options.html

CVE: CVE-2022-0018
Name: GlobalProtect App: Information Exposure Vulnerability When Connecting to GlobalProtect Portal With Single Sign-On Enabled
Description: An information exposure vulnerability exists in the Palo Alto Networks GlobalProtect app on Windows and MacOS where the credentials of the local user account are sent to the GlobalProtect portal when the Single Sign-On feature is enabled in the GlobalProtect portal configuration. This product behavior is intentional and poses no security risk when connecting to trusted GlobalProtect portals configured to use the same Single Sign-On credentials both for the local user account as well as the GlobalProtect login. However when the credentials are different, the local account credentials are inadvertently sent to the GlobalProtect portal for authentication. A third party MITM type of attacker cannot see these credentials in transit. This vulnerability is a concern where the GlobalProtect app is deployed on Bring-your-Own-Device (BYOD) type of clients with private local user accounts or GlobalProtect app is used to connect to different organizations. Fixed versions of GlobalProtect app have an app setting to prevent the transmission of the user's local user credentials to the target GlobalProtect portal regardless of the portal configuration. This issue impacts: GlobalProtect app 5.1 versions earlier than GlobalProtect app 5.1.10 on Windows and MacOS; GlobalProtect app 5.2 versions earlier than GlobalProtect app 5.2.9 on Windows and MacOS This issue does not affect GlobalProtect app on other platforms.
Severity: 6.5 (Medium)
CVSS: CVSS:3.1/AV:N/AC:L/PR:N/UI:R/S:U/C:H/I:N/A:N
Product: GlobalProtect
Affected Versions: 5.2.5
Mitigation: This issue is fixed in GlobalProtect app 5.1.10 on Windows and MacOS, GlobalProtect app 5.2.9 on Windows and MacOS, and all later GlobalProtect app versions with the force-disable-sso app setting.

Set force-disable-sso to yes to prevent unintended transmission of the local user credentials as described here:
https://docs.paloaltonetworks.com/globalprotect/10-1/globalprotect-admin/globalprotect-apps/deploy-app-settings-transparently/customizable-app-settings/app-behavior-options.html
Workarounds: 
There are no known workarounds for this issue.

Response:
Based on the provided CVE data, here are potential exploitation scenarios and recommended countermeasures for each vulnerability:

**CVE-2023-0009 & CVE-2024-9473 (GlobalProtect App: Local Privilege Escalation)**
Exploitation Scenario:
An attacker with local access to the system could exploit these vulnerabilities to escalate privileges and gain elevated access.
Countermeasures:
1. Update GlobalProtect app to a fixed version (5.2.13 or later) as soon as possible.
2. Limit user permissions to only those required for their job functions.

**CVE-2024-8687 (PAN-OS: Cleartext Exposure of GlobalProtect Portal Passcodes)**
Exploitation Scenario:
An attacker on the same network could capture traffic and learn the configured passcodes, allowing them to uninstall or disconnect GlobalProtect.
Countermeasures:
1. Update PAN-OS software to a fixed version as soon as possible.
2. Change passcodes regularly.
3. Implement workarounds provided in the CVE description.

**CVE-2021-3057 (GlobalProtect App: Buffer Overflow Vulnerability)**
Exploitation Scenario:
A man-in-the-middle attacker could disrupt system processes and potentially execute arbitrary code with SYSTEM privileges by exploiting this vulnerability.
Countermeasures:
1. Update GlobalProtect app to a fixed version as soon as possible.

**CVE-2022-0019 (GlobalProtect App: Insufficiently Protected Credentials)**
Exploitation Scenario:
A local attacker could obtain hashed credentials and authenticate as other users.
Countermeasures:
1. Update GlobalProtect app to a fixed version as soon as possible.
2. Limit user permissions to only those required for their job functions.

**CVE-2022-0016 (GlobalProtect App: Privilege Escalation When Using Connect Before Logon)**
Exploitation Scenario:
A local attacker could escalate privileges to SYSTEM or root by exploiting this vulnerability under certain circumstances.
Countermeasures:
1. Update GlobalProtect app to a fixed version as soon as possible.

**CVE-2023-6510 (Use after free in Media Capture in Google Chrome)**
Exploitation Scenario:
A remote attacker could potentially exploit heap corruption via specific UI interaction, leading to arbitrary code execution.
Countermeasures:
1. Update Google Chrome to the latest version as soon as possible.

**CVE-2022-0018 & CVE-2024-6990 (GlobalProtect App: Information Exposure Vulnerabilities)**
Exploitation Scenario:
An attacker could learn local user credentials or perform UI spoofing via crafted HTML pages.
Countermeasures:
1. Update GlobalProtect app and Google Chrome to fixed versions as soon as possible.
2. Implement the workarounds provided in the CVE descriptions.

**CVE-2023-5857 & CVE-2024-6999 (Inappropriate implementation in FedCM in Google Chrome)**
Exploitation Scenario:
An attacker could bypass discretionary access control or perform UI spoofing via crafted HTML pages.
Countermeasures:
1. Update Google Chrome to the latest version as soon as possible.

**CVE-2023-0006 (GlobalProtect App: Local File Deletion Vulnerability)**
Exploitation Scenario:
A user with elevated privileges could delete system files from the endpoint through a race condition.
Countermeasures:
1. Update GlobalProtect app to a fixed version as soon as possible.

**CVE-2024-7976 (Inappropriate implementation in FedCM in Google Chrome)**
Exploitation Scenario:
An attacker could perform UI spoofing via a crafted HTML page.
Countermeasures:
1. Update Google Chrome to the latest version as soon as possible.

For all vulnerabilities, it's essential to keep software up-to-date and implement security best practices such as limiting user permissions, using strong passwords, and applying workarounds when available. Regularly monitoring for potential threats is also crucial.

CVE: CVE-2024-9473
Name: GlobalProtect App: Local Privilege Escalation (PE) Vulnerability
Description: A privilege escalation vulnerability in the Palo Alto Networks GlobalProtect app on Windows allows a locally authenticated non-administrative Windows user to escalate their privileges to NT AUTHORITY/SYSTEM through the use of the repair functionality offered by the .msi file used to install GlobalProtect.
Severity: 7.8 (High)

Product: GlobalProtect

Customers who want to upgrade should reach out to customer support at  https://support.paloaltonetworks.com .

CVE: CVE-2024-8687
Name: PAN-OS: Cleartext Exposure of GlobalProtect Portal Passcodes
Description: An information exposure vulnerability exists in Palo Alto Networks PAN-OS software that enables a GlobalProtect end user to learn both the configured GlobalProtect uninstall password and the configured disable or disconnect passcode. After the password or passcode is known, end users can uninstall, disable, or disconnect GlobalProtect even if the GlobalProtect app configuration would not normally permit them to do so.
Severity: 7.1 (High)
CVSS: CVSS:3.1/AV:N/AC:L/PR:L/UI:N/S:U/C:L/I:N/A:H
Product: GlobalProtect
Affected Versions: 5.2.5
Mitigation: This issue is fixed in PAN-OS 8.1.25, PAN-OS 9.0.17, PAN-OS 9.1.16, PAN-OS 10.0.12, PAN-OS 10.1.9, PAN-OS 10.2.4, PAN-OS 11.0.1, and all later PAN-OS versions. It is also fixed in Prisma Access 10.2.9 and all later Prisma Access versions. To maintain GlobalProtect app functionality for the vulnerable features, we released a corresponding software update for GlobalProtect app 5.1.12, GlobalProtect app 5.2.13, GlobalProtect app 6.0.7, GlobalProtect app 6.1.2, and GlobalProtect app 6.2.1, and all later GlobalProtect app versions.

To maintain the ability for end users to use the uninstall password feature and the disable or disconnect passcode feature, you must ensure that you upgrade all GlobalProtect app deployments to a fixed version before you upgrade your PAN-OS software to a fixed version.

All fixed versions of GlobalProtect are backwards compatible with vulnerable versions of PAN-OS software. However, fixed versions of PAN-OS software are not backwards compatible with vulnerable versions of GlobalProtect.

You can find additional information for PAN-204689 here:  https://docs.paloaltonetworks.com/pan-os/11-1/pan-os-release-notes/pan-os-11-1-0-known-and-addressed-issues/pan-os-11-1-0-known-issues 

Prisma Access customers can open a support case to request an upgrade.
Workarounds: 
Change the following two settings (if enabled) to "Allow with Ticket":
* Network > GlobalProtect > Portals >  > Agent >  > App > Allow User to Disable GlobalProtect App
* Network > GlobalProtect > Portals >  > Agent >  > App > Allow user to disconnect GlobalProtect App

Change the following setting (if enabled) to "Disallow":
* Network > GlobalProtect > Portals >  > Agent >  > App > Allow User to Uninstall GlobalProtect App

CVE: CVE-2022-0019
Name: GlobalProtect App: Insufficiently Protected Credentials Vulnerability on Linux
Description: An insufficiently protected credentials vulnerability exists in the Palo Alto Networks GlobalProtect app on Linux that exposes the hashed credentials of GlobalProtect users that saved their password during previous GlobalProtect app sessions to other local users on the system. The exposed credentials enable a local attacker to authenticate to the GlobalProtect portal or gateway as the target user without knowing of the target users plaintext password. This issue impacts: GlobalProtect app 5.1 versions earlier than GlobalProtect app 5.1.10 on Linux. GlobalProtect app 5.2 versions earlier than and including GlobalProtect app 5.2.7 on Linux. GlobalProtect app 5.3 versions earlier than GlobalProtect app 5.3.2 on Linux. This issue does not affect the GlobalProtect app on other platforms.
Severity: 5.5 (Medium)
CVSS: CVSS:3.1/AV:L/AC:L/PR:L/UI:N/S:U/C:H/I:N/A:N
Product: GlobalProtect
Affected Versions: 5.2.5
Mitigation: This issue is fixed in GlobalProtect app 5.1.10 on Linux, GlobalProtect app 5.3.2 on Linux, and all later GlobalProtect app versions.

Existing credentials files that are exposed by this issue will be secured when the fixed GlobalProtect app is launched.
Workarounds: 
Users should not save their credentials until the GlobalProtect app is upgraded to a fixed version.

GlobalProtect portal administrators can prevent GlobalProtect app users from saving their credentials on the next connection to the GlobalProtect portal by preventing Save User Credentials from the portal agent configuration as described here:

https://docs.paloaltonetworks.com/globalprotect/10-1/globalprotect-admin/globalprotect-apps/deploy-app-settings-transparently/customizable-app-settings/user-behavior-options.html

CVE: CVE-2022-0018
Name: GlobalProtect App: Information Exposure Vulnerability When Connecting to GlobalProtect Portal With Single Sign-On Enabled
Description: An information exposure vulnerability exists in the Palo Alto Networks GlobalProtect app on Windows and MacOS where the credentials of the local user account are sent to the GlobalProtect portal when the Single Sign-On feature is enabled in the GlobalProtect portal configuration. This product behavior is intentional and poses no security risk when connecting to trusted GlobalProtect portals configured to use the same Single Sign-On credentials both for the local user account as well as the GlobalProtect login. However when the credentials are different, the local account credentials are inadvertently sent to the GlobalProtect portal for authentication. A third party MITM type of attacker cannot see these credentials in transit. This vulnerability is a concern where the GlobalProtect app is deployed on Bring-your-Own-Device (BYOD) type of clients with private local user accounts or GlobalProtect app is used to connect to different organizations. Fixed versions of GlobalProtect app have an app setting to prevent the transmission of the user's local user credentials to the target GlobalProtect portal regardless of the portal configuration. This issue impacts: GlobalProtect app 5.1 versions earlier than GlobalProtect app 5.1.10 on Windows and MacOS; GlobalProtect app 5.2 versions earlier than GlobalProtect app 5.2.9 on Windows and MacOS This issue does not affect GlobalProtect app on other platforms.
Severity: 6.5 (Medium)
CVSS: CVSS:3.1/AV:N/AC:L/PR:N/UI:R/S:U/C:H/I:N/A:N
Product: GlobalProtect
Affected Versions: 5.2.5
Mitigation: This issue is fixed in GlobalProtect app 5.1.10 on Windows and MacOS, GlobalProtect app 5.2.9 on Windows and MacOS, and all later GlobalProtect app versions with the force-disable-sso app setting.

Set force-disable-sso to yes to prevent unintended transmission of the local user credentials as described here:
https://docs.paloaltonetworks.com/globalprotect/10-1/globalprotect-admin/globalprotect-apps/deploy-app-settings-transparently/customizable-app-settings/app-behavior-options.html
Workarounds: 
There are no known workarounds for this issue.

Response:
## Analysis of Palo Alto Networks GlobalProtect App Vulnerabilities

Based on the provided CVE data for version 5.2.5 of the GlobalProtect app, several potential exploitation scenarios exist:

**High Severity Exploits:**

* **CVE-2023-0009 (Local Privilege Escalation):** An attacker with local access could exploit this vulnerability to gain elevated privileges on the system. Mitigation requires upgrading to version 5.2.13, 6.0.5, 6.1.1, or later.
* **CVE-2024-9473 (Local Privilege Escalation):** This vulnerability allows a local user with limited access to elevate privileges to NT AUTHORITY/SYSTEM.  Mitigation involves upgrading to version 6.2.5 or later.
* **CVE-2021-3057 (Buffer Overflow Vulnerability):** A man-in-the-middle attacker could exploit this vulnerability to disrupt system processes and potentially execute arbitrary code with SYSTEM privileges. Mitigation requires upgrading to GlobalProtect app 5.1.9 on Windows, 5.2.8 on Windows and Universal Windows Platform, or 5.3.1 on Linux.
* **CVE-2022-0016 (Privilege Escalation when using Connect Before Logon):** This vulnerability allows a local attacker to escalate privileges under certain circumstances. Mitigation requires upgrading to GlobalProtect app 5.2.9 on Windows and macOS, or later versions.

**Medium Severity Exploits:**

* **CVE-2022-0018 (Information Exposure when using Single Sign-On):** While this vulnerability doesn't directly allow code execution, it exposes sensitive user credentials under specific circumstances (like BYOD scenarios). Mitigation involves setting the 'force-disable-sso' app setting.
 

* **CVE-2024-6999 and CVE-2024-7976 (UI Spoofing in FedCM):** Remote attackers could potentially trick users into interacting with malicious elements through UI spoofing. Mitigation involves upgrading to Google Chrome versions later than 128.0.6613.84

**Important Considerations:**


* **Prioritize High Severity Vulnerabilities:** Address the high-severity vulnerabilities (CVE-2023-0009, CVE-2024-9473, CVE-2021-3057) first as they pose the greatest risk.
* **Patching is Essential:** Regularly update the GlobalProtect app and Google Chrome to the latest versions to mitigate known vulnerabilities.
* **Implement Security Best Practices:**  Use strong passwords, enable multi-factor authentication, and restrict user privileges based on need.

**Google Chrome Vulnerabilities:**

While not directly related to the GlobalProtect app, several CVEs listed affect Google Chrome versions prior to 127.0.6533.88. It is crucial to update your browser regularly to protect against these vulnerabilities.


Remember that this analysis is based on the provided CVE information. Conducting a thorough security assessment and penetration testing can reveal additional vulnerabilities specific to your environment.

CVE: CVE-2022-0019
Name: GlobalProtect App: Insufficiently Protected Credentials Vulnerability on Linux
Description: An insufficiently protected credentials vulnerability exists in the Palo Alto Networks GlobalProtect app on Linux that exposes the hashed credentials of GlobalProtect users that saved their password during previous GlobalProtect app sessions to other local users on the system. The exposed credentials enable a local attacker to authenticate to the GlobalProtect portal or gateway as the target user without knowing of the target users plaintext password. This issue impacts: GlobalProtect app 5.1 versions earlier than GlobalProtect app 5.1.10 on Linux. GlobalProtect app 5.2 versions earlier than and including GlobalProtect app 5.2.7 on Linux. GlobalProtect app 5.3 versions earlier than GlobalProtect app 5.3.2 on Linux. This issue does not affect the GlobalProtect app on other platforms.
Severity: 5.5 (Medium)
CVSS: CVSS:3.1/AV:L/AC:L/PR:L/UI:N/S:U/C:H/I:N/A:N
Product: GlobalProtect
Affected Versions: 5.2.5
Mitigation: This issue is fixed in GlobalProtect app 5.1.10 on Linux, GlobalProtect app 5.3.2 on Linux, and all later GlobalProtect app versions.

Existing credentials files that are exposed by this issue will be secured when the fixed GlobalProtect app is launched.
Workarounds: 
Users should not save their credentials until the GlobalProtect app is upgraded to a fixed version.

GlobalProtect portal administrators can prevent GlobalProtect app users from saving their credentials on the next connection to the GlobalProtect portal by preventing Save User Credentials from the portal agent configuration as described here:

https://docs.paloaltonetworks.com/globalprotect/10-1/globalprotect-admin/globalprotect-apps/deploy-app-settings-transparently/customizable-app-settings/user-behavior-options.html

CVE: CVE-2024-8687
Name: PAN-OS: Cleartext Exposure of GlobalProtect Portal Passcodes
Description: An information exposure vulnerability exists in Palo Alto Networks PAN-OS software that enables a GlobalProtect end user to learn both the configured GlobalProtect uninstall password and the configured disable or disconnect passcode. After the password or passcode is known, end users can uninstall, disable, or disconnect GlobalProtect even if the GlobalProtect app configuration would not normally permit them to do so.
Severity: 7.1 (High)
CVSS: CVSS:3.1/AV:N/AC:L/PR:L/UI:N/S:U/C:L/I:N/A:H
Product: GlobalProtect
Affected Versions: 5.2.5
Mitigation: This issue is fixed in PAN-OS 8.1.25, PAN-OS 9.0.17, PAN-OS 9.1.16, PAN-OS 10.0.12, PAN-OS 10.1.9, PAN-OS 10.2.4, PAN-OS 11.0.1, and all later PAN-OS versions. It is also fixed in Prisma Access 10.2.9 and all later Prisma Access versions. To maintain GlobalProtect app functionality for the vulnerable features, we released a corresponding software update for GlobalProtect app 5.1.12, GlobalProtect app 5.2.13, GlobalProtect app 6.0.7, GlobalProtect app 6.1.2, and GlobalProtect app 6.2.1, and all later GlobalProtect app versions.

To maintain the ability for end users to use the uninstall password feature and the disable or disconnect passcode feature, you must ensure that you upgrade all GlobalProtect app deployments to a fixed version before you upgrade your PAN-OS software to a fixed version.

All fixed versions of GlobalProtect are backwards compatible with vulnerable versions of PAN-OS software. However, fixed versions of PAN-OS software are not backwards compatible with vulnerable versions of GlobalProtect.

You can find additional information for PAN-204689 here:  https://docs.paloaltonetworks.com/pan-os/11-1/pan-os-release-notes/pan-os-11-1-0-known-and-addressed-issues/pan-os-11-1-0-known-issues 

Prisma Access customers can open a support case to request an upgrade.
Workarounds: 
Change the following two settings (if enabled) to "Allow with Ticket":
* Network > GlobalProtect > Portals >  > Agent >  > App > Allow User to Disable GlobalProtect App
* Network > GlobalProtect > Portals >  > Agent >  > App > Allow user to disconnect GlobalProtect App

Change the following setting (if enabled) to "Disallow":
* Network > GlobalProtect > Portals >  > Agent >  > App > Allow User to Uninstall GlobalProtect App

-----
CVE: CVE-2022-0018
Name: GlobalProtect App: Information Exposure Vulnerability When Connecting to GlobalProtect Portal With Single Sign-On Enabled
Description: An information exposure vulnerability exists in the Palo Alto Networks GlobalProtect app on Windows and MacOS where the credentials of the local user account are sent to the GlobalProtect portal when the Single Sign-On feature is enabled in the GlobalProtect portal configuration. This product behavior is intentional and poses no security risk when connecting to trusted GlobalProtect portals configured to use the same Single Sign-On credentials both for the local user account as well as the GlobalProtect login. However when the credentials are different, the local account credentials are inadvertently sent to the GlobalProtect portal for authentication. A third party MITM type of attacker cannot see these credentials in transit. This vulnerability is a concern where the GlobalProtect app is deployed on Bring-your-Own-Device (BYOD) type of clients with private local user accounts or GlobalProtect app is used to connect to different organizations. Fixed versions of GlobalProtect app have an app setting to prevent the transmission of the user's local user credentials to the target GlobalProtect portal regardless of the portal configuration. This issue impacts: GlobalProtect app 5.1 versions earlier than GlobalProtect app 5.1.10 on Windows and MacOS; GlobalProtect app 5.2 versions earlier than GlobalProtect app 5.2.9 on Windows and MacOS This issue does not affect GlobalProtect app on other platforms.
Severity: 6.5 (Medium)
CVSS: CVSS:3.1/AV:N/AC:L/PR:N/UI:R/S:U/C:H/I:N/A:N
Product: GlobalProtect
Affected Versions: 5.2.5
Mitigation: This issue is fixed in GlobalProtect app 5.1.10 on Windows and MacOS, GlobalProtect app 5.2.9 on Windows and MacOS, and all later GlobalProtect app versions with the force-disable-sso app setting.

Set force-disable-sso to yes to prevent unintended transmission of the local user credentials as described here:
https://docs.paloaltonetworks.com/globalprotect/10-1/globalprotect-admin/globalprotect-apps/deploy-app-settings-transparently/customizable-app-settings/app-behavior-options.html
Workarounds: 
There are no known workarounds for this issue.
CWE IDs: CWE-200

**Vulnerabilities in Google Chrome**

The following vulnerabilities were identified in **Google Chrome** across multiple versions (114.0.5665.138):

### 1. Medium Severity Vulnerability
- **CVE:** CVE-2023-2931  
- **Name:** Use after free in PDF in Google Chrome prior to 114.0.5735.90  
- **Description:** Allowed a remote attacker to potentially exploit heap corruption via a crafted PDF file, which could allow unintended transmission of local user credentials or create potential security risks related to ADB (All Day Battle).  
- **Severity:** Medium  
- **CVSS Score:** N/A  
- **Affected Versions:** 114.0.5665.138  
- **Mitigation:** No known workarounds are available for this issue.

---

### 2. High Severity Vulnerability
- **CVE:** CVE-2024-5831  
- **Name:** Use after free in Dawn in Google Chrome prior to 126.0.6478.54  
- **Description:** Allowed a remote attacker to potentially exploit heap corruption via a crafted HTML page, which could allow command execution or privilege escalation.  
- **Severity:** High  
- **CVSS Score:** CVSS:3.1/AV:N/AC:L/PR:N/UI:R/S:U/C:H/I:H/A:H  
- **Affected Versions:** 114.0.5665.138  
- **Mitigation:** Ensure that all GlobalProtect app versions are upgraded to a fixed version.
